<p><strong><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Baba Times Digest | 2 December 2014 17.12 EST | New York Edition</span></span></span><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;"></span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;"></span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;"></span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;"></span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><br style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;" /></span></span></strong></p>

</xml><![endif]--><!--[if gte mso 10]>
<![endif]--> </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Sri Gita Jayanti<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Divine Life Society Publication: </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/religions/gita_siva.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Hindu Fasts and Festivals</b></span></a></span><b> by Sri Swami Sivananda<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">THE HOLY <i>Gita </i>Jayanti, or the birthday of the <i>Bhagavad Gita, </i>is celebrated throughout India by all the admirers and lovers of this most sacred scripture on the eleventh day (Ekadashi) of the bright half of the month of Margaseersha (December-January), according to the Hindu almanac. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The message of the <i>Bhagavad Gita, </i>given by the Lord Himself on the battlefield of Kurukshetra even now illumines the path of humanity on its onward march to perfection.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The <i>Gita </i>is the most beautiful and the only truly philosophical song. Its teachings are based on the sacred <i>Upanishads</i>. It contains sublime lessons on wisdom and philosophy. It is the "Song Celestial". It is the universal gospel. It contains the message of life that appeals to all, irrespective of race, creed, age or religion.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The <i>Gita </i>shows a way to rise above the world of duality and the pairs of opposites, and to acquire eternal bliss and immortality. It is a gospel of action. It teaches the rigid performance of one's duty in society, and a life of active struggle, keeping the inner being untouched by outer surroundings, and renouncing the fruits of actions as offerings unto the Lord.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The <i>Gita </i>is a source of power and wisdom. It strengthens you when you are weak, and inspires you when you feel dejected and feeble. It teaches you how to resist unrighteousness and follow the path of virtue and righteousness.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The <i>Gita </i>is not merely a book or just a scripture. It is a living voice carrying an eternally indispensable and vital message to mankind. Its verses embody words of wisdom coming from the infinite ocean of knowledge, the Absolute Itself.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The voice of the <i>Gita </i>is the call of the Supreme. It is the divine sound explained. The primal source of all existence, all power, is the manifested soundOm. This is the Divine Word. It is Nada Brahman, whose unceasing call is: "Be ye all ever merged in the eternal, unbroken, continuous consciousness of the Supreme Truth." This is the sublime message that the <i>Gita</i> elaborates and presents in all comprehensiveness and in a universally acceptable form. </span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">To be always conscious of the Divine, to ever feel the Divine Presence, to live always in the awareness of the Supreme Being in the chambers of your heart and everywhere around you, is verily to live a life of fullness and divine perfection on earth itself. Such a constant remembrance of God and such an attitude of mind will release you forever from the clutches of illusion and free you from all fear. To forget the Supreme is to fall into illusion. To forget Him is to be assailed by fear. To live in unbroken remembrance of the Supreme Truth is to remain always in the region of light, peace and bliss, far beyond the reach of illusion and delusion.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Mark carefully how the <i>Gita </i>stresses again and again this lofty message.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The Lord declares: "Keep thou thy mind in Me, in Me place thy reason".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">In another verse He says: "Therefore, at all times remember Me and fight. You will surely attain Me, having thus offered yourself".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">And yet again: "Perform thou action, remaining united with Me at heart".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The <i>Gita </i>guides you to glory with the watchwords: "Be thou divine-minded, devoted to Me as your goal, and let your subconscious mind be divine".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The Lord gives the following firm assurance also: "I become the saviour from this mortal world for those whose minds are set on Me".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Such is the most illuminating message of the <i>Gita, </i>seeking to lead man to a life of perfection even while performing his ordained role here. Long has this message been neglected by man. Forgetting the Lord, the world has turned towards sense indulgence and mammon. A terrible price has been paid. O man, enough of this forgetfulness! The Lord has warned you against heedlessness: "If, out of egoism, thou wilt not hear, then thou shalt perish".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Live in the spirit of the teachings of the <i>Gita. </i>Mere talks or lectures will not help you in any way. Put into practice the teachings of this most sacred scripture and attain eternal bliss and peace.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The <i>Gita </i>may be summarised in the following seven verses:</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">1. "Uttering the one-syllabled Om, the Brahman, and remembering Me, he who departs, leaving the body thus, attains the Supreme Goal".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">2. "It is meet, O Lord, that the world delights and rejoices in Thy praise; the demons fly in fear to all quarters, and all the hosts of Siddhas bow to Thee!"</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">3. "With hands and feet everywhere, with eyes, heads and mouths everywhere, with ears everywhere, He exists in the world, enveloping all".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">4. "Whosoever meditates on the omniscient, ancient ruler of the whole world, minuter than an atom, the supporter of all, of form inconceivable, effulgent like the sun, such a one goeth beyond the darkness of ignorance".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">5. "They, the wise, speak of the indestructible Asvattha, having its roots above and branches below, whose leaves are the metres or hymns; he who knows it is a knower of the <i>Vedas".</i></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">6. "And I am seated in the hearts of all; from Me are memory and knowledge, as well as their absence. I am verily that which has to be known by all the <i>Vedas</i>; I am indeed the author of Vedanta, and the knower of the <i>Vedas </i>am I".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">7. "Fix thy mind on Me; be devoted to Me; sacrifice to Me; bow down to Me; having thus united thy whole Self with Me, taking Me as the Supreme Lord, thou shalt verily come to Me".</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Read the whole of the <i>Gita </i>on Sundays and other holidays. Study carefully again and again the verses in the second discourse, which deal with the state of the Sthitaprajna (a perfected Yogi and sage). Also study the eight nectarine verses in the twelfth discourse.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The study of the <i>Gita </i>alone is sufficient for the purpose of scriptural study. You will find in it a solution to all your problems. The more you study it with devotion and faith, the deeper will your knowledge become, the more penetrative would be your insight, and the clearer your thinking. Even if you live in the spirit of one verse of the <i>Gita, </i>all your miseries will come to an end and you will attain the goal of lifeimmortality and eternal peace.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Take a resolve on <i>Gita </i>Jayanti that you will read at least one discourse every day. Recite the fifteenth discourse before taking your meals. This is done at the Sivananda Ashram.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Keep a pocket-sized edition of the <i>Gita </i>with you at all times. Mark a few verses in it which inspire you. Everyday, while you wait for your bus or train, or whenever you have a little leisure, pull out the book and read these verses. You will be ever inspired.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">May you all lead the life taught by the <i>Gita! </i>May the <i>Gita, </i>the blessed Mother of the <i>Vedas, </i>guide and protect you! May it nourish you with the milk of the ancient wisdom of the <i>Upanishads</i>!</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Glory to Lord Krishna, the Divine Teacher! Glory to Sri Vyasa, the poet of poets, who composed the <i>Gita! </i>May his blessings be upon you all!</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;">&nbsp;</p>
<p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: .0001pt; line-height: normal;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><span class="MsoHyperlink"><b>Excerpts from: </b></span><b>Sri Gita Jayanti - </b><span style="color: #0000ff;"><a href="http://www.dlshq.org/religions/gita_siva.htm"><span style="color: #0000ff;"><b>Hindu Fasts and Festivals</b></span></a></span></span><b><span style="font-size: 9.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"> by Sri Swami Sivananda</span><o:p></o:p></span></b></p>
